Jamison Brereton

47 (488)
Soma, Indra, etc.
Garga Bh─Бradv─Бja
31 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except br╠еhat─л 19, anuс╣гс╣нubh 23, g─Бyatr─л 24, dvipad─Б 25, jagat─л 27
Like III.53, the family hymn of the Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras, dedicated primarily to Indra and placed at the end of the Indra cycle in Maс╣Зс╕Нala III, this hymn is the family hymn of the Bharadv─Бjas, dedicated primarily to Indra and also positioned at the end of the Indra cycle in its maс╣Зс╕Нala. Also like III.53, VI.47 consists of a number of smaller units, some of which seem to have little or no connection with each other. Different scholars have suggested different divisions of the hymn; our own is based in great part on arguments based on rhetoric.834 VI.47
It begins with an extravagant praise of soma (vss. 1тАУ5), rhetorically unified by the oft-repeated pronoun тАЬthis one hereтАЭ (ay├бm), which in several of its occurrences takes an unusual final position (as opposed to its standard initial slot). With the presence of soma unquestionably established, Indra is then invited to drink it in the following verse (6), with the ritual context explicitly identified as the Midday Pressing. In fact already toward the end of the soma verses, there has been a modu
lation toward Indra: several of the deeds attributed to тАЬthis one hereтАЭ are more Indraic than Somian, especially the propping of heaven in 5cd, and the final words of verse 5 тАЬthe bull accompanied by the MarutsтАЭ would ordinarily uniquely identify Indra, who is addressed in the next p─Бda (6a).
The extended middle section of the hymn (vss. 7тАУ21) is entirely devoted to Indra. Verses 7тАУ10 contain a series of direct pleas, for Indra to lead us forward to wider space and a better life and to provide refreshment and a good life. The next three verses (11тАУ13) are similarly general, but couched in the 3rd person. (Two of these verses [12тАУ13] are repeated in a very late hymn, X.131.6тАУ7, and in turn are used in the later Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л ritual, but we see no direct evidence of that ritual here.) Indra appears in these verses as a sort of universal protector and helper. This character
ization seems to raise questions in the poetтАЩs mind: if Indra is the protector of all, then how does any particular group get ahead?
This implicit question prompts the next, somewhat jarring, section of the hymn (vss. 14тАУ19), which concerns the fickle and unpredictable way in which IndraтАЩs patronage flits from one man to another. The section begins undramatically by announcing the many verbal and ritual offerings to Indra, coming (it seems) from many different groups (vs. 14), all seeking his aid. The next verse (15) seems to treat IndraтАЩs capriciousness as a positive trait: he doesnтАЩt only and always aid the strong, but will frequently promote a man who has fallen behind. The next two verses (16тАУ 17) continue this theme, but with IndraтАЩs behavior appearing in a darker light, as he arbitrarily breaks his agreements and betrays his followers. In the following verse (18) Indra is infinitely multiplied, presenting a different appearance to each differ
ent group and seemingly possessed of a thousand horses, each pair of which might take him to a different group pleading for his aid. This somewhat disturbing section is brought to a happy end in verse 19: only one pair of horses is yoked (to bring Indra to us?), the various forms are under Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs control, and in the rhetorical question that forms the second half-verse (matching the question in vs. 15) it is concluded that Indra is unlikely to stay with the enemy when our own patrons are now providing such a good sacrifice. One of the most notable aspects of this little section (esp. vss. 15тАУ18) about IndraтАЩs constantly changing behavior is its grammati cal reflection: these verses are packed with ─Бmreс╕Нita nominal compounds тАЬeach x, x after xтАЭ and so-called тАЬintensiveтАЭ verb forms (really iterative-frequentative, mean
ing тАЬkeeps x-ing, continually x-esтАЭ), forms that are relatively marked in the Vedic grammatical system. The presence of four ─Бmreс╕Нitas and four intensives in four verses both calls attention to the message and reflects it by portraying a regularly alternating set of actions and objects. The reassurance of verse 19 has come none too soon, for in verse 20 the poet and his group find themselves in a bad spot, not the wide and bountiful place they prayed Indra to lead them to in verses 7тАУ8. In verse 21 the opposing forces are over come (by Indra, it seems, though he is unnamed). Thus, verses 7тАУ8 and 20тАУ21 form a larger ring around the Indra section.
A d─Бnastuti follows (vss. 22тАУ25), in which the victorious kings distribute the bounty won in the battle referred to in verse 21. The d─Бnastuti proceeds briskly and efficiently, without any of the jocularity commonly found in d─Бnastutis elsewhere, just a list of the acquisitions.
The last part of the hymn (vss. 26тАУ31) is the strangest. It consists of three verses (26тАУ28) addressed to the war chariot and three (29тАУ31) addressed to the war drum. These verses are also found in the Atharvaveda (VI.125тАУ126). Each of these martial objects is praised in the most extravagant terms and compared with the attributes of the gods. Although this section seems to have no direct connection with the rest of the hymn, it may have been attached to the hymn (or even originally composed as part of it) in response to the battle depicted in verses 20тАУ21 and the distribution of booty in verses 22тАУ25. Chariots are part of the gift (24a), and it would not be surprising that a war drum might be allotted as part of the post-battle distribution. It is also worth remembering that in III.53, the family hymn of the Vi┼Ыv─Бmitras mentioned above, one of the final sections (vss. 17тАУ20) is devoted to the possible perils besetting a chariot and its team, with phraseology similar to verses 26тАУ28 in this hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra _________ 01-05 As indicated in the published introduction, the first 5 vss. of the hymn constitute a praise of soma, shading, towards the end, into simultaneous praise of Indra. It is formally unified: beginning with vs. 2, all but one (2cd) of the hemistichs begins with ay├бm, and vs. 1 contains four exx. of ay├бm as well (2 each in the 1st 2 p─Бdas), though oddly positioned.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSavoury indeed is this (Soma); sweet is it, sharp, and full of flavour; no one is able to encounter Indra in battles after he has been quaffing this (Soma).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Sweet is this one, certainly, and it is honeyed; sharp is this one, certainly, and it is full of sap.
And now that Indra has drunk of it, no one at all overcomes him at the challenges.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although this vs. is quite straightforward in general, it has some peculiarities. To begin with, the four nominal clauses with ay├бm in the first hemistich are all in the unusual order X ay├бm, which is reversed (/repaired) in the four subsequent vss. See esp. the opening of 1a sv─Бd├║с╣г k├нl─Бy├бm corrected to the more standard 2a ay├бс╣Г sv─Бd├║с╕е. I have no idea what motivated the X ay├бm order.

It is not clear to me whether the four clauses name four different types/preparations of soma or all four refer to a single soma (or, in some way, both: all soma drinks, no matter how prepared, are in essence one).

Note also the particle k├нla, which is rare in the RV, esp. outside of X: only 5 of the 12 occurrences are not in X, and 2 of them are in this vs. I am also puzzled by the accent on asy├б in c. Since the soma is amply referred to earlier in the vs., we would expect unaccented asya (cf., e.g., papiv─Бm╠Р├нndro asya V.29.3, 30.11). I have no explanation, and it seems not to have bothered any other commentator.

Griffith

YEA, this is good to taste and full of. sweetness, verily it is strong and rich in flavour.
No one may conquer Indra in the battle when he hath drunken of the draught we offer.

Geldner

Der ist gewi├Я schmackhaft und der ist s├╝├Я; der ist gewi├Я scharf und der ist w├╝rzig. Und wenn Indra von diesem getrunken hat, so zwingt ihn keiner mehr zum Kampfe.

Grassmann

Recht s├╝ss f├╝rwahr und honigreich ist dieser, recht scharf f├╝rwahr, und reich an Saft der Soma; Und nimmer kann, wenn Indra ihn getrunken, ihn einer je besiegen in den K├дmpfen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe savoury Soma, drunk on this occasion, has been most exhilarating; by drinking of it Indra has been elevated to the slaying of Vс╣Ыtra, and it has destroyed the numerous hosts of ┼Ъambara and the ninetynine cities.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dehyaс╕е = dehiс╕е;

Digdhaс╕е = smeared or plural stered, implying puriс╕е, cities, as if thy consisted of stucoed or plural stered houses

Jamison Brereton

This sweet one here was the most exhilarating, on which Indra became exhilarated for the smashing of Vr╠еtra,
he who (having performed) many exploits smashed apart the nine and ninety walls of ┼Ъambara.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. chains rel. clauses, with the gen. rel. y├бsya in b referring to the soma in a, while nom. y├бс╕е in cd refers to Indra, who first appears in the rel. cl. of b.

It is difficult (though perhaps not impossible) to construe v├н тАж h├бn тАШsmash apartтАЩ with the acc. cyautn─Б╠БтАШexploitsтАЩ in c as well as the more likely object dehy├ас╕е тАШwallsтАЩ in d. It is therefore best to follow Geldner (also Hoffmann, Injunk. 168) and supply a form of тИЪkс╣Ы or the like in c.

Griffith

This sweet juice here had mightiest power to gladden: it boldened Indra when he siaughtered Vrtra,
When he defeated Sambara’s many onslaughts, and battered down his nineand ninety ramparts.

Geldner

Dieser s├╝├Яe hier war der berauschendste, an dem sich Indra im Vritrakampf berauscht hat, der viele Taten getan, des Sambara neunundneunzig Mauern zerschlagen hat.

Grassmann

Der s├╝sse hier ist’s, der am meisten Rausch schafft, von dem Indra im Vritrakampf berauscht war, Als er des ├Зambara vielfache Werke, die neunundneunzig W├дlle schlug in St├╝cke.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Soma inspires my speech; this develops the desired intelligence; this sagacious (Soma) has created the six vast conditions, from which no creature is distinct.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Six vast conditions: heaven, earth, day, night, water, and plural nts

Jamison Brereton

This one, when it is drunk, rouses my speech; it has awakened an eager inspired thought.
This wise one measured out the six broad (realms), from which no world is at a distance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is not clear what noun to supply with fem. pl. urv─л╠Бс╕е, though something like тАШworlds (so Geldner), realmsтАЩ makes sense. The same с╣г├бс╕Н urv─л╠Бс╕е is found in X.14.16 in unclear context, and as a voc. in X.128.5 d├йv─лс╕е с╣гaс╕Н urv─лс╕е ‘you six broad goddessesтАЩ, again with uncertain referent. Elsewhere urv─л╠Бс╕е applies to waters or rivers, but liquid doesnтАЩt seem appropriate here. Perhaps in our vs. itтАЩs evoking a pl. of pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б тАШearthтАЩ, with a pun on a different word for тАШbroadтАЩ, ur├║-, urv─л╠Б-. Note that pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б- occurs in the next vs., dependent on varim├бn- тАШexpanseтАЩ, which is derivationally related to ur├║-.

03-05 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction. as well as above, the praise of soma modulates towards praise of Indra in this sequence, starting in the 2nd half of vs. 3. The first half of 3 clearly identifies soma as referent with the ppl. p─лt├бс╕е тАШwhen drunkтАЩ, but the cosmogonic deeds of 3d and of at least the first half of 4 begin to sound Indraic. We are brought abruptly back to soma in 4d (s├│mo d─Бdh─Бra), but this almost seems like a trick or a feint to keep us from drifting further. And vs. 5 again sounds Indraic, esp.

the final vс╣Ыс╣гabh├│ mar├║tv─Бn тАЬthe bull accompanied by the MarutsтАЭ: mar├║tvant- is overwhelmingly an epithet of Indra. For a similar nearby sequence of vss. that oscillates between soma and Indra (and also uses ay├бm as an organizing word) see VI.44.22-24 and comm. ad loc.

Griffith

This stirreth up my voice when I have drunk it: this hath aroused from sleep my yearning spirit.
This Sage hath measured out the six expanses from which no single creature is excluded.

Geldner

Dieser treibt getrunken mir die Rede hervor, dieser hat den willigen Gedanken geweckt. Dieser Weise ma├Я die sechs weiten Welten aus, au├Яer denen keine Welt besteht.

Grassmann

Getrunken reget dieser mir das Wort auf, und hat geweckt das sehnsuchtsvolle Lied mir; Sechs Weiten hat der weise abgemessen, von denen fern kein Wesen ist zu finden.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis it is which formed the expanse of the earth, the compactness of the heaven; this Soma has deposited the ambrosia in its three principal (receptacles), and has upheld the spacious firmament.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three principal receptacles: plural nt, water and cows; has upheld the spacious: Soma as the moon and Soma as a product; cf. svamim─Б oс╣гadh─лс╕е vi┼Ыv─Бstv─Бmapo ajanayastvam g─Бс╕е tvam─Б tatanthorvantarikс╣гam: RV 1.091.22

Jamison Brereton

This is the one who created the expanse of the earth; who created the height of heaven is this one here;
this one (created) the beestings on the three slopes [=worlds?]. Soma upheld the broad midspace.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich has a repetitive structure inside a chiastic frame. The opening ay├бс╣Г s├б y├бс╕е is balanced by ay├бс╣Г s├бс╕е at the end of b; we might perhaps expect *y├│ ay├бс╣Г s├бс╕е in fact. The single verb ├бkс╣Ыс╣Зot, inside this frame, does for both objects, which are responsive: morphologically identical and near-rhyming acc. varim─Б╠Бс╣Зam тАж varс╣гm─Б╠Бс╣Зam, each with a dependent gen. belonging to a matched semantic pair, pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е тАж div├бс╕е.

P─Бda c is problematic. It lacks a verb, so it is impossible to know for sure what relations are envisioned among the ill-assorted lexical items; the real-world referents of p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гam тАШbeestingsтАЩ and tisс╣Ы╠Бс╣гu prav├бtsu тАЬon/in the three slopesтАЭ are uncertain; it is not even clear whether it should be grouped with ab or with d. Geldner groups it loosely with d, renders p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гam as тАЬSeimтАЭ and tisс╣Ы╠Бс╣гu prav├бtsu as тАЬin die drei Str├╢men,тАЭ and supplies тАЬhat тАж geschaffenтАЭ as the verb. I am not sure what heтАЩs trying to convey, and prav├бt- does not straightforwardly mean тАШstreamтАЩ, but тАШslopeтАЩ or тАШplungeтАЩ. The published translation takes c with ab, supplying ├бkс╣Ыс╣Зot from there, but I am now doubtful about this, in part on the basis of IX.109.6 div├│ dhart─Б╠Бsi ┼Ыukr├бс╕е p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гah тАЬYou, the gleaming beestings, are the supporter of heaven,тАЭ where soma is identified as p─лy┼л╠Бс╣гa- and identified as an upholder (dhart├бr-), reminiscent of our d s├│mo d─Бdh─Бra. As for tisс╣Ы╠Бс╣гu prav├бtsu, I wonder if this is shorthand for тАЬprav├бt- plus twoтАЭ as expressed in VII.50.4 prav├бto niv├бta udv├бtaс╕е тАЬ(from) the slope, the depth, and the heightтАЭтАФpossibly referring to the three worlds, which all appear in this verse: heaven and earth in ab, the midspace in d. Perhaps the idea is that Soma placed or supports the distillation of himself, his liquid essence, in all three worlds. If this is so, a form of тИЪdhс╣Ы borrowed from d would work better than тИЪkс╣Ы from ab.

I also now realize that the preterital tr. of d─Бdh─Бra in d, matching that of Geldner (тАЬhat тАж befestigtтАЭ), is wrong, since, as K├╝mmel points out, the pf. of тИЪdhс╣Ы is always presential.

Putting this all together, I would alter the tr. of cd to тАЬthis one (upholds) his тАШbeestingsтАЩ in the three тАЬslopesтАЭ (=worlds); Soma upholds the broad midspace,тАЭ with absolutely no certainty about the rendering of c.

03-05 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction. as well as above, the praise of soma modulates towards praise of Indra in this sequence, starting in the 2nd half of vs. 3. The first half of 3 clearly identifies soma as referent with the ppl. p─лt├бс╕е тАШwhen drunkтАЩ, but the cosmogonic deeds of 3d and of at least the first half of 4 begin to sound Indraic. We are brought abruptly back to soma in 4d (s├│mo d─Бdh─Бra), but this almost seems like a trick or a feint to keep us from drifting further. And vs. 5 again sounds Indraic, esp.

the final vс╣Ыс╣гabh├│ mar├║tv─Бn тАЬthe bull accompanied by the MarutsтАЭ: mar├║tvant- is overwhelmingly an epithet of Indra. For a similar nearby sequence of vss. that oscillates between soma and Indra (and also uses ay├бm as an organizing word) see VI.44.22-24 and comm. ad loc.

Griffith

This, even this, is he who hath created the breadth of earth, the lofty height of heaven.
He formed the nectar in three headlong rivers. Soma supports the wide mid-air above us.

Geldner

Dieser ist es, der die Breite der Erde, dieser ist es, der die H├╢he des Himmels schuf. Dieser hat in den drei Str├╢men den Seim geschaffen: Soma hat den weiten Luftraum gefestigt.

Grassmann

Er ist es, der der Erde Breite ausmass, und der des Himmels hohe W├╢lbung baute; Er hielt des Meeres Biestmilch an drei Halden, den weiten Luftkreis Soma fest zusammen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis makes known the wonderfully beautiful and inspiring (solar) radiance) at the appearance of the dawns, whose dwelling is the firmament; this mighty (Soma) has sustained the heaven with a powerful support, th sender of rain, the leader of the winds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This one found the flood with its brilliant appearance at the (fore)front of the dawns with their gleaming seats.
This one, great, with a great pillar propped up heavenтАФhe, the bull, accompanied by the Maruts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition divide the 2nd hemistich as тАж sk├бmbhanen├│d # di y─Б╠Бm, with ├║d the final of p─Бda a and di y─Б╠Бm distracted and p─Бda-initial. But this is clearly wrong: ├║d is a preverb in tmesis with astabhn─Бt and should open the p─Бda, and dy─Б╠Бm is rarely if ever distracted. LubotskyтАЩs division is correct.

As noted above, the 2nd hemistich of this vs. sounds esp. Indraic.

03-05 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction. as well as above, the praise of soma modulates towards praise of Indra in this sequence, starting in the 2nd half of vs. 3. The first half of 3 clearly identifies soma as referent with the ppl. p─лt├бс╕е тАШwhen drunkтАЩ, but the cosmogonic deeds of 3d and of at least the first half of 4 begin to sound Indraic. We are brought abruptly back to soma in 4d (s├│mo d─Бdh─Бra), but this almost seems like a trick or a feint to keep us from drifting further. And vs. 5 again sounds Indraic, esp.

the final vс╣Ыс╣гabh├│ mar├║tv─Бn тАЬthe bull accompanied by the MarutsтАЭ: mar├║tvant- is overwhelmingly an epithet of Indra. For a similar nearby sequence of vss. that oscillates between soma and Indra (and also uses ay├бm as an organizing word) see VI.44.22-24 and comm. ad loc.

Griffith

He found the wavy sea of brilliant colours in forefront of the Dawns who dwell in brightness.
This Mighty One, the Steer begirt by Maruts, hath propped the heavens up with a mighty pillar.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHero, Indra, who are the slayer of foes in contests for (the acquisition of) treasures, drink boldly from the pitcher; drink copiously at the noonday rite; receptacle of rices, bestow riches upon us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Boldly drink the soma in the tub, IndraтАФas smasher of Vr╠еtra at the confluence of goods, o champion.
At the Midday Pressing, drench yourself. Standing amid wealth, establish wealth in us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

rayi-sth─Б╠Бna- is a bahuvr─лhi, lit. тАШhaving your place/standing in wealthтАЩ vel sim., though the published translation is less awk.

Griffith

Drink Soma boldly from the beaker, Indra, in war for treasures, Hero, Vrtra-slayer!
Fill thyself full at the mid-day libation, and give us wealth, thou Treasury of riches.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLike one who goes before us, Indra, (on the road), look out, bring before us infinite wealth; be our conductor beyond the bounds (of want), convey us safely over (peril); be our careful guide, our gude to desirable (affluence).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Look out: pra с╣Зaс╕е pura eteva pa┼Ыya, like one who is preceding us, look; look after the travellers under the charge of the m─Бrgarakс╣гaka, the protector of the road, an escort, or perhaps, the leader of a k─Бfil─Б

Jamison Brereton

Indra, look forward for us, like the man who goes ahead; lead us further forward, toward a better state.
Become one of good passage, who gives us passage beyond; become one of good guidance and valued guidance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. is built on variant repetition: ab pr├б с╣Зah тАж, pr├б naс╕е тАж prataram / c su-p─Бr├│ ati-p─Бray├│ / d s├║-n─лtiс╕е тАж v─Бm├б-n─лtiс╕е.

I have no idea why in the identical sequence pr├б + naс╕е, the first has retroflexed с╣З and the latter does not. Both pr├б-s are preverbs in tmesis with 2nd sg.

impvs. (pa┼Ыya and naya). The only differences are 1) the first pr├б sequence is not initial (being preceded by voc. ├нndra), 2) in the second sequence the impv.

immediately follows naс╕е, while in the first some verbal material intervenes, and 3) in the first naс╕е functions as a dat. but in the second as an acc. None of these differences should (as far as I can see) trigger different sandhi effects.

Griffith

Look out for us, O Indra, as our Leader, and guide us on to gain yet goodlier treasure.
Excellent Guardian, bear us well through peril, and lead us on to wealth with careful guidance.

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Indra, who are wise, conduct us to the spacious world (of heaven), to a blessed state of happiness, light, and safety; may we recline in the graceful, protecting, and mighty arms of you the ancient one.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Lead us along to a wide world, as the one who knowsтАФto sun-filled light, to fearlessness, to well-being.
High are the arms of you who are stalwart, Indra. Might we approach these two lofty shelters.

Lead us to ample room, O thou who knowest, to happiness, security, and sunlight.
High, Indra, are the arms of thee the Mighty: may we betake. us to their lofty shelter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬplural ce us, possessor of riches, in your ample chariot, (behind) your powerful horses; bring to us from among all viands the most excellent food; let not, Maghavan, any opulent man surpass us in wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Place us in the widest chariot box, Indra, on the two best-pulling horses, you possessor of hundreds.
Convey hither the highest refreshment of refreshments. Let our (refreshment) not cross over to the тАЬriches of the stranger,тАЭ
bounteous one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. contains three phonologically similar splvs., stationed at p─Бda edge: #v├бriс╣гс╣нhe … #v├бhiс╣гс╣нhayoс╕е … / … v├бrс╣гiс╣гс╣нh─Бm#. This is somewhat reminiscent of the phonological/morphological figure in 4ab varim─Б╠Бс╣Зam тАж varс╣гm─Б╠Бс╣Зam, esp. since v├бriс╣гс╣нhe and v├бrс╣гiс╣гс╣нh─Бm belong to the same roots as the two forms in 4.

In b the Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition text should read ┼Ыat─Бvann. This voc. is variously interpr. (see Oldenberg for some reff.), but I follow Geldner, and implicitly the Pp., in taking it as (metrically) lengthened *┼Ыata-van, to a -van-stem, contra GrassmannтАЩs ┼Ыata-ava(n)t-, with the pres. part.

of тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ. This ┼Ыat─Б-van- would be a byform of better attested ┼Ыat├б-vant-. It needs to belong to a -van- rather than a -vant- stem because otherwise the expected voc. would be -vas. But we find -vant- and -van- stems side-by-side, notably in magh├бvan(t)-. Debrunner (AiG II.2, most clearly p. 904, citing this passage) argues that -vant-stems are тАЬsachlichтАЭ while -van-stems are тАЬpers├╢nlich,тАЭ which would work for ┼Ыat├бvant- versus our ┼Ыat─Бvan-, but not, obviously, for magh├бvan(t)-.

The tr. of d is disputed. Geldner takes r─Б╠Бyaс╕е as nom. pl. (as it generally is) and the subj. of the sg. verb t─Бr─лt: тАЬnicht sollen die Reicht├╝mer eines hohen Herren die unseren ├╝berbieten.тАЭ This requires that the sg. verb take a masc. pl. subj. While the neut. pl. + sg. verb construction is fairly rare, but attested and inherited, I do not know of masculine pl. equivalents. Oldenberg (ZDMG 54: 170) thinks the incongruity of number is the result of the adjustment to the formulaic nature of r─Б╠Бyo ary├бс╕е, tr.

тАЬm├╢gen uns nicht die Kargen den Reichtum ├╝berwinden,тАЭ with ary├бс╕е nom. pl. of ar├н-

– in other words a different masc. pl. subj. with sg. verb. Thieme (Fremdling, 56-57) makes appropriately short work of both of these proposals, but I find his own solution puzzling: тАЬM├╢ge nicht ├╝berholen unsere Reicht├╝mer [der] des Fremdlings.тАЭ Since he adamantly rejects the masc. pl. + sg. verb interpr., all I can figure is that heтАЩs generating a singular *ray├нс╕е to serve as subject (represented by his bracketed [der]), but there is no support for this and it seems an artifice of convenience. No doubt mine does, too: like Thieme I take r─Б╠Бyaс╕е as acc. pl., as it sometimes is (though r─Бy├бс╕е would be expected), and for sg. subj. I supply ├нс╣г- тАШrefreshmentтАЩ from the previous p─Бda. I also interpr. the verb t─Бr─лt not as hostile тАШovercomeтАЩ but as a plain verb of motion тАШcross over toтАЩ; cf. usages like ├бt─Бriс╣гma t├бmasaс╕е p─Б╠Бram asy├б тАЬwe have crossed over to the far shore of this darknessтАЭ (I.92.6 = I.183-84.6, VII.73.1).

The point is that the refreshment weтАЩve begged Indra for should not fall into enemy hands. As discussed esp. ad IV.48.1 and VI.14.3, 20.1, I take the phrase r─Б╠Бyo ary├бс╕е тАЬriches of the strangerтАЭ as referring to manpower.

Griffith

Set us on widest chariot-seat, O Indra, with two steeds best to draw, O Lord of Hundreds!
Bring us the best among all sorts of viands: let not the foe’s wealth, Maghavan, subdue us.

Uns setz auf weiten Wagensitz, o Indra, auf schnellstes Rossepaar, o h├╝lfereicher; Fahr Trank herbei, der Tr├дnke allerbesten, nicht raub’ ein Feind, o Indra, unsre Habe.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMake me happy, Indra; be plural ased to prolong my life; shapen my intellect like the edge of a metal sword; whatsoever, desirous (of propitiating) you, I may utter, be plural ased by it; render me the object of divine protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, be gracious. Seek a means of life for me. Spur on my poetic vision like a blade of copper.
Whatever I say here in devotion to you, just this enjoy. Make me accompanied by the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the simile in b, see VI.3.5.

Griffith

Be gracious, Indra, let my days be lengthened: sharpen my thought as ’twere a blade of iron
Approve whatever words I speak, dependent on thee, and grant me thy divine protection.

Geldner

тАЬI invoke, at repeated sacrifice, Indra, the preserver, the protector, the hero, who is easily propitiated, Indra, the powerful, the invoked of many; may Indra, the lord of affluence, bestow upon us prosperity.тАЭ

I call on Indra, the able one, called on by many. Let bounteous Indra establish well-being for us.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the protecting, opulent Indra be the bestower of felicity by his protections; may he, who is all-knower of felicity by his protections; may he, who is all-knowing, foil our adversaries; may he keep us out of danger, and may we be the possessors of excellent posterity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let Indra be of good protection, of good help with his help, very gracious, affording all possessions.
Let him thrust away hatred; let him create fearlessness. Might we be lords of good heroes in abundance.

Whitney

Translation

  1. Let Indra be well-saving, well-aiding with aids, very gracious,
    all-possessing; let him put down (b─Бdh) hatred, let him make for us
    fearlessness; may we be lords of wealth in heroes.

Notes
This hymn and the following are two successive verses in RV. (x. 131. 6,
7, or vi. 47. 12, 13), and are also found together in VS. (xx. 51, 52),
TS. (i. 7. 13тБ┤тБ╗тБ╡), and MS. (iv. 12. 5). All these agree in leaving out
the nas which disturbs the meter of c. Our pada-text agrees with
that of RV. in both verses in falsely dividing sv├бре░v─Бn, and the comm.
explains the word correspondingly with dhanav─Бn hit─Бtm─Б v─Б.

Keith

Indra, the protector, the granter of aid with his aids;
All knowing, be kindly to us;
Let him restrain the enemy, let him make security,
May we be lords of strength [4].

Griffith (AV)

May Indra with his help, Lord of all treasures, be unto us a careful protector. Drive off our foes and give us peace and safety. May we be lords of goodly store of heroes.

Griffith

May helpful Indra as our good Protector, Lord of all treasures, favour us with succour,
Baffle our foes, and give us rest and safety, and may we be the lords of hero vigour.

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрдГ рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡реЗрджрд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛрд╜рд╡реЛрднрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕реБрдореГрд│реАрдХреЛ рднрд╡рддреБ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реЛ рдмрд╛рдзрддрд╛рдорднрдпрдВ рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рдпрдВ рдкрддрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рддрд╕реНрдп рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрд╛ рдпреВрдпрдордкрд┐ рднрд╡рдд реерезреирее

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢реЛ рднрд╡реЗрддреНрддрд╕реНрдп рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреИрдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпреЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрддрд╛рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ (рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдмрд╣рд╡рдГ рд╕реНрд╡реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ (рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ (рд╕реБрдореГрд│реАрдХрдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░рдГ (рднрд╡рддреБ) (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ) рдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдВ рд╡реЗрддреНрддрд┐ (рдмрд╛рдзрддрд╛рдореН) рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдпрддреБ (рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдГ) рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рджреЛрд╖рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрднрдпрдореН) рднрдпрд░рд╛рд╣рд┐рддреНрдпрдореН (рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдХрд░реЛрддреБ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╢реЛрднрдирдВ рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдВ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдореЛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдВ рдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдп (рдкрддрдпрдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рдХрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирдГ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) реерезреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рд╜рдЦрд┐рд▓рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдГ рдХреГрддрдкреВрд░реНрдгрдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреЛ рдмрд╣реБрдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╡рдЪреНрдЫреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╕реНрдп рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХреЛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╕реНрдп рджрдгреНрдбрдХреГрддреНрд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдирд┐рд░реНрднрдпрддрд╛рдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдп рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ реерезреирее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреЛ ! рдЬреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛, рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЕрдиреЗрдХ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдЕрд╕рд▓реЗрд▓рд╛ рд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рддрдГрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ, рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдВрдирд╛ рджрдВрдб рджреЗрдгрд╛рд░рд╛, рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рдирд┐рд░реНрднрдп рдЕрд╕рддреЛ рддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резреи рее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ (рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ) рд╕рдм рдзрдирд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдпрд╛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рд╕реБрдореГрдбреАрдХрдГ)рд╕реБрдЦрдж (рднрд╡рддреБ) рд╣реЛ (рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдГ) рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ (рдмрд╛рдзрддрд╛рдореН) рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░реЗ (рдЕрднрдпрдВ рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдЕрднрдп рдХрд░реЗ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд╕реБрдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдХреЗ (рдкрддрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣рдо рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рееремрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдпрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╕реБрдЦрдкреНрд░рдж рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХрд╛ рдирд╛рд╢рдХ рдЕрднрдп рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдпрд╛ рд╣реЛред рд╕реБрдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдФрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╢рд░реАрд░ рд╕рджрд╛ рдмрдирд╛рдпреЗ рд░рдЦрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рееремрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдГ рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН тАЬрд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреНтАЭ [рдЛреж ремредрекренредрезреи рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдзрдирдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реБрдореГрд│реАрдХрдГ-рднрд╡рддреБ) рд░рдХреНрд╖рдгреИрдГ рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рд╕реБрдЦрджреЛ рднрд╡рддреБ (рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдГ-рдмрд╛рдзрддрд╛рдореН) рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреДрдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдирд╛рд╢рдпрддреБ (рдЕрднрдпрдВ рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдЕрднрдпрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдкрддрдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реБрдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдордмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрд╡рддрдГ рд╢рд░реАрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдиреЛ рднрд╡реЗрдо рееремрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ред

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕реБрддреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛) рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ, (рд╕реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдмрд╣реБрдд рд╕реЗ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд┐ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛, (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡реЗрджрд╛рдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд рдзрди рд╡рд╛ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ (рдЕрд╡реЛрднрд┐рдГ) рдЕрдиреЗрдХ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдУрдВ рд╕реЗ (рд╕реБрдореГрдбреАрдХрдГ) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рд╕реБрдЦ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рднрд╡рддреБ) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗред рд╡рд╣ (рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдГ) рд╡реИрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдмрд╛рдзрддрд╛рдореН) рд╣рдЯрд╛рд╡реЗ, (рдирдГ) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдЕрднрдпрдореН) рдирд┐рд░реНрднрдпрддрд╛ (рдХреГрдгреЛрддреБ) рдХрд░реЗ рдФрд░ рд╣рдо (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдХреЗ (рдкрддрдпрдГ) рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерезрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

English translation:

тАЬMay we continue in the favour of that adorable (deity) even in his auspicious good-will; may that protecting and opulent Indra drive far from us, into extinction, all those who hate us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might we be in the favor of him who deserves the sacrifice, in his propitious benevolence.
Let Indra of good protection, of good help to us keep hatred away even from a distance. с│У

Keith

May we enjoy the favour of him the worshipful,
And also his loving kindness;
May the protector Indra, the granter of aid,
For ever fend far from us the enemy.

Griffith

May we enjoy the grace of him the Holy, yea, may we dwell in his auspicious favour.
May helpful Indra as our good Preserver drive from us, even from afar, our foemen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo you the praises and prayers of the worshipper hasten like a torrent down a declivity; and you thunderer, aggregate the immense wealth (of sacrificial offerings), copious libations, and milk, and the Soma.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Apo g─Бс╕е yuvase samind┼лn: apo = vasat─лvar─л which is said by K─Бty─Бyana S┼лtra 8.9.7-10 to be portions of water taken from a running stream on the evening previous to the ceremony, and kept in jars in different parts of the sacrificial chamber, to be mixed with the Soma; cf. Taittir─лya Yajus., Prap─Бс╣нhaka III. Anuv─Бka XII).

Jamison Brereton

Down to you, Indra, run the hymns and the sacred formulations as teams, like a wave along the slopes.
As broad as your bounty are the many pressings. You join together the waters, the cows, and the drops, you possessor of the mace.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The long vowel of ur┼л╠Бis puzzling. Since it appears in the simile ur┼л╠Бn├б r─Б╠Бdhaс╕е, it should be neut. sg. ur├║, and acdg. to Grassmann and AiG III.145 (with reff.) it is, with metrical lengthening. By contrast, Lubotsky identifies it as a nom. pl. Since the frame corresponding to this simile is neut. pl. s├бvan─Бni pur┼л╠Бni, I also prefer neut. pl.; it may show attraction to the number of the frame: тАЬthe many pressings are broad like your bounty.тАЭ As Geldner (n. 14d) cleverly points out, the waters, cows, and drops are the three ingredients of soma.

Griffith

Like rivers rushing down a slope, O Indra, to thee haste songs and prayers and linked verses.
Thou gatherest, Thunderer! like widespread bounty, kine, water, drops, and manifold libations.

Geldner

Zu dir, Indra, eilen wie die Wellen ihre Bahnen so die Lobreden, die Segensworte, die Gaben. Ausgedehnt wie eine Schenkung sind die vielen Somaspenden. Du nimmst die Wasser, Kuhmilch, die Somas├дfte f├╝r dich in Beschlag, o Keulentr├дger.

Grassmann

Zu dir hin str├╢men, wie vom Abhang Wellen, Gebete, Indra, Lieder, Spruchgespanne, Du spannst dir an als reichen Lohn, o Blitzer, viel Spenden, Wasser, Milch und Indutr├дnke.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWho may (adequately) praise him? Who may satisfy him? Who offer worthy adoration? Since Maghava is daily conscious of his own terrible (power); by his acts he makes first one and then the other precede and follow, as (a man) throws out his feet (alternately in walking).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Make first one and then: that is, Indra, at his plural asure, makes the first of his worshippers the last, and the last the first

Jamison Brereton

Who will praise him, who will fill him, who will sacrifice to him, if the bounteous one would always help only the strong?
Like one who puts down his two feet one after the other, with his powers he makes the one who was behind to be in front.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner renders d exactly opposite to the published translation: тАЬso macht er den Vorderen zum HintermannтАЭ (fld. by Klein, тАЬ─Бmreс╕НitasтАЭ: тАЬhe makes the one at the fore into one who lags behindтАЭ). But the simile in c is about walking one step at a time (тАЬputting his two feet down one after the otherтАЭ), and unless Indra is walking backwards my interpr. must be correct. ItтАЩs true that p┼л╠Бrvam тАШin frontтАЩ precedes ├бparam тАШbehindтАЩ in the text, but word order is scarcely a reliable guide in the RV, esp. since in nominal sentences we often get PREDICATE SUBJECT order. (Furthermore, there’s a sort of iconic ordering of the two adjectives, with p┼л╠Бrva- first, which can be independent of the larger sense.)

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this section, which concerns IndraтАЩs fickle attentions to various clients in turn, is marked grammatically by ─Бmreс╕Нitas and intensives (i.e., iterative/frequentatives), expressing the constantly shifting nature of the actions and their objects. See the published introduction. for the continuity of content I see in this section.

Griffith

Who lauds him, satisfies him, pays him worship? E’en the rich noble still hath found him mighty.
With power, as when one moves his feet alternate, he makes the last precede, the foremost follow.

Geldner

Wer m├╢chte ihn preisen, wer ihm spenden, wer opfern, wenn der Gabenreiche allezeit nur den Gewaltigen beg├╝nstigte? Wie man die F├╝├Яe einen um den anderen vorsetzt, so macht er den Vorderen zum Hintermann durch seine Macht.

Grassmann

Wer preist ihn recht, wer s├дttigt, wer verehrt ihn, dass auch dem starken stets der m├дcht’ge helfe? Wie F├╝sse setzend, einen vor den andern, l├дsst m├дchtig er den vordern hinten bleiben.

English translation:

тАЬThe hero Indra is renowned; humiliating every formidable (foe), and repeatedly changing the plural ce of one (worshipper) with that of another; Indra, the enemy of the arrogant, the soverign of both (heaven and earth), calls again and again (to encourage) the men who are his worshippers.тАЭ

keeps prodding the clans, the sons of ManuтАФfirst one, then
the other.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреАрджреГрд╢реЛ рднрд╡реЗрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡реЗ) (рд╡реАрд░рдГ) рд╢реМрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгреЛрдкреЗрддрдГ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдореБрдЧреНрд░рдореН) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдВ рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡рд┐рдирдореН (рджрдорд╛рдпрдиреН) рджрдордирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН (рдЕрдиреНрдпрдордиреНрдпрдореН) рднрд┐рдиреНрдирдВ рднрд┐рдиреНрдирдореН (рдЕрддрд┐рдиреЗрдиреАрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ) рднреГрд╢рдВ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдиреН (рдПрдзрдорд╛рдирджреНрд╡рд┐рдЯреН) рдпреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рд╕рдГ (рдЙрднрдпрд╕реНрдп) рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╕рдореБрджрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп (рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛) рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╡рд┐рдирдпрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирдГ (рдЪреЛрд╖реНрдХреВрдпрддреЗ) рднреГрд╢рдорд╛рд╣реНрд╡рдпрддрд┐ (рд╡рд┐рд╢рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдГ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдпрдзрд░рдГ (рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреН) реерезремрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra rejects the friendship of those who are formost (in pious acts), and, depositing them, associates with (their) inferiors; or (again) shaking off those who neglect his worship, Indra abides many years with those who serve him.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He twists away from his partnerships with those in front; continually double-crossing them, he goes with those behind.
Indra keeps enduring through the many autumns, shaking them
[=autumns] off so they donтАЩt close in.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The p┼л╠Бrva-/├бpara- binary returns from 15, but here I think it not only refers to those ahead and behind positionally (as there), but also has a temporal sense (not represented in the published translation): his previous allies in p─Бda a he dumps in favor of newer ones in b.

The hapax ├бn─Бnubh┼лt─лс╕е is not entirely clear, but two things must be kept in mind: 1) itтАЩs a fem. pl., presumably acc.; 2) its sense must be derived from ├бnu тИЪbh┼л, which generally means тАШcome close to, give way toтАЩ. Because of 1), it should modify ┼Ыar├бdaс╕е тАШautumnsтАЩ, a fem. cons. stem (so Geldner). But GeldnerтАЩs rendering тАЬdass sie an ihm nicht wahrgenommen werdenтАЭ seems distant in sense from the verbal lexeme; OldenbergтАЩs тАЬ(alles) Sichnichtanschliessen тАжтАЭ seems closer. I take the cmpd as a bahuvr─лhi meaning тАШhaving no intimacyтАЩ and interpr. it as proleptic in an expression of purpose: Indra shakes off the years so that they do not come close/attach themselves to him.

(GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdass sie тАж nicht тАжтАЭ has the same proleptic purpose interpr.) The point is that one canтАЩt get old if one keeps the years at a distance; my тАЬclose inтАЭ is meant to capture the slangy tone of the passage (see also тАЬdouble-crossтАЭ in b).

He loves no more the men he loved aforetime: he turns and moves away allied with others.
Rejecting those who disregard his worship, Indra victorious lives through many autumns.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, the prototype, has assumed various forms, and such is his form as that which (he adopts) for his manifestation; Indra, multiform by his illusion, proceeds (to his many worshippers), for the horses, yoked to his car are a thousand.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra has assumed: Indra presents himself as Agni, Viс╣гс╣Зu, or Rudra, or any other deity who is the actual object of worship, and is really the deity tobe adored; he is identifiable with each; Horses yoked: Indra’s chariots and horses are multiplied according to the forms in which he manifests himself; Indra is here identified with Parame┼Ыvara, the supreme first cause, identical with creation

Jamison Brereton

He has a form corresponding to every form; this form of his is for display.
Indra keeps going about in many forms through his magical powers, for ten hundred fallow bays are yoked for him.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. concerns IndraтАЩs shape-shifting propensity, enabled by his m─Бy─Б╠Б-.

It is a slightly more complex formulation of III.53.8 r┼лp├бm-r┼лpam magh├бv─Б bobhav─лti, m─Бy─Б╠Бс╕е krс╣З╠е v─Бn├бs tanv├аm p├бri sv─Б╠Бm тАЬForm after form the bounteous one assumes, wrapping his own body in tricks.тАЭ Although pr├бtir┼лpo babh┼лva should lit.

mean тАЬhe has become one having a form corresponding тАж,тАЭ this seemed awkward.

Geldner thinks the form in b is IndraтАЩs true form, to be recognized behind the various disguises in p─Бda a; by contrast, I think each form Indra assumes is meant for display and none of them is the тАЬrealтАЭ one. pr├бti тИЪcakс╣г is the lexeme used for the display of the girl at the svayaс╣Гvara; see its use with Dawn in I.113.11 and 124.8.

Each constituency is shown a different formтАФhence the ─Бmreс╕Нita r┼лp├бс╣Г-r┼лpam in a and the thousand horses in d, which presumably take each different form of Indra in a different direction.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, this section, which concerns IndraтАЩs fickle attentions to various clients in turn, is marked grammatically by ─Бmreс╕Нitas and intensives (i.e., iterative/frequentatives), expressing the constantly shifting nature of the actions and their objects. See the published introduction. for the continuity of content I see in this section.

Griffith

In every figure he hath been the mode: this is his only form for us to look on.
Indra moves multiform by his illusions; for his Bay Steeds are yoked, ten times a hundred.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYoking his horses to his car, Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б shines in many plural ces here in the three worlds; who (else), sojourning daily among his present worshippers, is their proector against adversaries?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In this с╣Ыca,Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б is an appellative of Indra, the ancient artificer!

Jamison Brereton

Having yoked the two fallow bay mares to his chariot, Tvaс╣гс╣нar rules over the many (forms) here.
Who will always sit on the side of the hostileтАФand especially when
(our) patrons are sitting (a sacrificial session)?

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. makes a small ring with vs. 15, both containing k├бс╕е + SUBJUNCTIVE. The fact that this vs. is in a different meter (Bс╣Ыhat─л, not Triс╣гс╣нubh) from the whole hymn that precedes it may also signal the end of a section. As indicated in the published introduction, I think this vs. is meant as reassurance: in contrast to the endlessly multiplying Indra of vs. 18 (and the fickle Indra of the previous vss.), Tvaс╣гс╣нar has now taken control, yoking only a single team (for IndraтАЩs journey, in my opinion) and exerting his dominion over forms, thus reining in IndraтАЩs excess shape-shifting.

Although the word r┼лp├б- does not appear in the vs., it can be easily supplied with bh┼л╠Бri on the basis of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs well-known role as shaper of forms (cf. Macdonell, Ved.

Myth. 116, and passages like I.188.9, VIII.10.28, X.100.9, 184.1).

The 2nd hemistich poses a rhetorical question about Indra (unnamed): why would Indra stick by the enemy when our sacrifice is so appealing? We are essentially urging him to switch sides again, and since he does so frequently, we have hope of succeeding. Assuming that p├бkс╣гa in sandhi represents p├бkс╣гaс╕е (so Pp), it belongs to a neut.

s-stem found only here in the RV, but attested in AV and elsewhere. This requires us to allow an acc. with тИЪ─Бs тАШsitтАЩ, rather than the usual loc. There is no warrant to emend the accent to pakс╣г├б and take it as a loc. to the -├б-stem.

P─Бda d constitutes a loc. abs., with the part. ─Б╠Бs─лna- used pregnantly for тАШsitting (a sattra)тАЩ. The introductory ut├б is curious, since there is nothing it can conventionally conjoin. Klein (DGRV 45-56) classifies it with the unclassifiable residue of ut├б forms, tr. it тАШespeciallyтАЩ. The published translation follows this tack. However, I think we can derive it from the standard uses of ut├б тАШandтАЩ. English has an idiom in which тАШandтАЩ is used to add as an afterthought what the speaker considers the clinching, but somewhat off-topic, circumstantial argument – as in a sequence like тАЬwhy would he break up with her now– and with her just graduated?тАЭ

Griffith

Here Tvastar, yoking to the car the Bay Steeds, hath extended sway.
Who will for ever stand upon the foeman’s side, even when our princes sit at ease?

Seine beiden Falbinnen an den Wagen spannend schaltet Tvastri hier viel. Wer wird allezeit sich auf die Seite des Feindes schlagen, zumal wann die freigebigen G├╢nner eine Opfersitzung halten?

Grassmann

Die goldfarbenen beiden Stuten sich anschirrend, ergl├дnzet Tvaschtar pr├дchtig hier. Wer sitzt gelassen stets, auch an des Feindes Seite, wie bei den Priestern, welche um ihn sitzen?

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWe have wandered, gods, into a desert where there is no track of cattle; the vast extant earth has become the protectress of murderers; direct us, Bс╣Ыhaspati, in our search for cattle; show the path, Indra, to your votary being astray.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Garga, the author of this s┼лkta, is said to have lost his way in a desert; he repeated this с╣Ыca to Bс╣Ыhaspati and Indra, who enabled him to regain his road; no track of cattle: agavy┼лti kс╣гetram = gosa├▒cararahitam de┼Ыam, a plural ce devoid of the grazing of cattle

рдЕрдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕рджреНрдордирдГ рд╕рджрдирд╛рддреН рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рджрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реИрдХрджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдЬрд╛рдГ рдЬрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреНрдордирд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрднрд╡рдиреН ‘рд╕рджреГрд╢реАрдГ рддреБрд▓реНрдпрд░реВрдкрд╛рдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реАрдГ рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рдореН рдЕрдк рдЕрд╕реЗрдзрддреН рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрдпрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердореН ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдзрдореН рдЕрд╣рд░рд░реНрдзрдореН рдЕрдкрд░рдВ рднрд╛рдЧрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдпрд┐рддреБрдореН ред рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрдордХрд╕реНрдп рджрд┐рд╡рд╕рд╕реНрдп рд╣рд┐ рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рд░реЗрдХреЛ рднрд╛рдЧрдГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╡реГрд╖рднрдГ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдпрд┐рддрд╛ рд╕ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рджрд╛рд╕рд╛ рджрд╛рд╕реМ рдЙрдкрдХреНрд╖рдкрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░реМ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд╕реНрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд╛ ред рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдВ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рд╣реЗрддреБрднреВрддрдВ рдзрдирдореН ред рддрджрд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреМ рд╡рд░реНрдЪрд┐рдирдВ рд╢рдореНрдмрд░рдВ рдЪ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╡рд╕реБрд░реМ рдЙрджрд╡реНрд░рдЬреЗ ред рдЙрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реНрд░рдЬрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпреБрджрд╡реНрд░рдЬреЛ рджреЗрд╢рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдЕрд╣рдиреН рд╣рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, becoming manifest from his abode (in the firmament), dissipates, day by day, the resembling glooms, (so that he may distinguish) the other portion, (or the day); and the showerer has slain the two wealth-seeking slaves, Varcin and ┼Ъambara, in (the country of) Udavraja.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Udavraja, de┼Ыa vi┼Ыeс╣гaс╕е, a sort of country, one into which the waters flow, udak─Бni vrajantyasmin

Jamison Brereton

Day after day he drove off from their seat the other half, the black kindred all of the same appearance.
The bull smashed the two D─Бsas, mercenaries, Varcin and ┼Ъambara, at the moated place.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My tr. differs conceptually and syntactically from GeldnerтАЩs, also, to a lesser degree, from SchmidtтАЩs (Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra 83). Geldner thinks the obj. sadс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы─лс╕е тАж kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е тАж j─Б╠Бс╕е refers to the nights (тАЬdie тАж gleichen (N├дchte), die schwarzen KinderтАЭ) and that any├бm ├бrdham тАЬthe other sideтАЭ is the goal to which Indra drove the nights. Acdg. to him, this is a different image of the singerтАЩs Not – the first narrowness, the second unbroken night. I find the supposed change of topic, from the tight place in which we found ourselves in vs. 20, unlikely; instead I consider this vs. a continuation of vs. 20, in which Indra drives away the enemy, as often described as black or dark, that implicitly hemmed us in, a view shared by Schmidt. However, the latter agrees with Geldner in taking any├бm ├бrdham as a goal, тАЬT├дglich vertrieb er die gleichen schwarzen Kinder von ihrem Sitz an die andere (Welt-)H├дlfte,тАЭ whereas I consider it a characterization of the enemy and so in apposition to sadс╣Ы╠Б┼Ы─лс╕е тАж kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е тАж j─Б╠Бс╕е, the phrase into which itтАЩs interleaved. The тАЬother halfтАЭ would be the alternately favored and disfavored sides in vss. 15-18, as well as the тАЬside of the hostileтАЭ (dviс╣гat├бс╕е p├бkс╣гaс╕е) of 19c.

Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition disassemble the sandhi across cd as vasnay├бnta, but this dual must have a long final; so Pp.

The part. vasnay├бnt─Б is a hapax, but related to vasn├б- тАШpriceтАЩ, v├бsnya- тАШto be sold, up for saleтАЩ. It modifies the two enemies of Indra, Varcin and ┼Ъambara, of whom we know little beyond IndraтАЩs enmity towards them. The denom. vasna-y├б- is therefore interpretable in a number of ways. Grassmann takes it as тАШfeilschenтАЩ (haggle), while Geldner tr. тАШL├╢segeld fordernтАЩ (demand ransom), calling the two enemies Raubritter (robber barons) in his introduction. (p. 144). EWA posts both tr., though they do not seem at all equivalent to me. Schmidt returns to GrassmannтАЩs feilschen. I add yet another possibility -

  • тАШmercenariesтАЩ – on the basis of a literal rendering of normal denom. semantics тАШseek XтАЩ, hence тАШseek a priceтАЩ. But given the state of our ignorance about these two foes, no interpr. is secure (though I very much doubt that the two were тАШhagglingтАЩ with Indra when he picked up his vajra). We should note that in the next vs. (22c), we accept тАЬthe goods belonging to ┼ЪambaraтАЭ (┼Ы─Бmbar├бс╣Г v├бsu), which may refer to ┼ЪambaraтАЩs vasn├б- in 21, though not in a way that disambiguates it.

Grassmann takes ud├бvraje as a PN, Geldner as a place name. My tr. follows SchmidtтАЩs interpr. (83-84) as a bahuvr─лhi тАШdessen H├╝rde das Wasser istтАЩ, as a description of a mountain surrounded (or semi-surrounded) by a body of water.

Day after day far from their seat he drove them, alike, from place to place, those darksome creatures.
The Hero slew the meanly-huckstering Dasas, Varcin and Sambara, where the waters gather.

Er vertrieb die Tag f├╝r Tag gleichen N├дchte, die schwarzen Kinder, aus ihrem Sitz nach der anderen Seite. Der Bulle erschlug die beiden L├╢segeld fordernden Dasa┬┤s, den Yarcin und Sambara in Udavraja.

Er vertrieb t├дglich die einander gleichenden dunkeln Wesen von ihrem Sitze weg nach der andern H├дlfte [der Nacht]; der Stier erschlug die feilschenden D├дmonen, die Flutversperrer [ich lese ud├бvraj─Б] Vartschin und ├Зambara.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ ! рдпрдерд╛ рдЬрд╛рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреЛ рджрд┐рд╡реЗрджрд┐рд╡реЗ рд╕рджреГрд╢реАрдГ рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдпрдорд░реНрдзрдВ рдЪрд╛рд╜рд╕реЗрдзрддреН рд╕рджреНрдордиреЛрд╜рдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдордкрд╛рд╕реЗрдзрджреН рд╡реГрд╖рдн рдЙрджрд╡реНрд░рдЬреЗ рд╡рд░реНрдЪрд┐рдирдВ рд╢рдореНрдмрд░рдорд╣рдБрд╕реНрддрдерд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрдирдпрдиреНрддрд╛ рджрд╛рд╕рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддреЗрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдореН реереирезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдПрддрджрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБ рдЪрддрд╕реГрд╖реБ рд╕реГрдЮреНрдЬрдпрдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреЛрдХрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮреЛ рджрд╛рдирд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГред рд╕ рдПрд╡ рджрд┐рд╡реЛрджрд╛рд╕реЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рдереЛрд╜рддрд┐рдерд┐рдЧреНрд╡ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрддреЗ ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд░рд╛рдзрд╕рдГ рдЖрд░рд╛рдзрдпрд┐рддреБрдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреБрдГ ред рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдереНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареА ред рддреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡рддреЗ рдорд╣реНрдпрдВ рдЧрд░реНрдЧрд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреЛрдХрдГ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рджрд╢ рдХреЛрд╢рдпреАрдГ рд╕реБрд╡рд░реНрдгрдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреН рджрд╢рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдиреН рдХреЛрд╢рд╛рдиреН рджрд╢ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рдиреБ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореН рдЕрджрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреН ред рдЗрддреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ ред рд╡рдпрдВ рдЪ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рджрд┐рд╡реЛрджрд╛рд╕рд╛рддреН рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреЛрдХрд╛рддреН рд╡рд╕реБ рдзрдирдВ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧреНрд░рднреАрд╖реНрдо рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдореНред рдЕрддрд┐рдерд┐рдЧреНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рддрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреЛрдХрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рднреВрддрдВ рд░рд╛рдзрдГ рд░рд╛рдзрдХрдВ рд╢рд╛рдореНрдмрд░рдВ рд╢рдореНрдмрд░рджрд╕реБрд░рд╛рджрд╛рдЧрддрдореН ред рд╢рдореНрдмрд░рдВ рд╣рддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рджрддреНрддрдВ рддрджреАрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPrastoka has given to your worshipper, Indra, ten purses of gold, and ten horses, and we have accepted this treasure from Divod─Бsa, the spoil won by Atithigva from ┼Ъambara.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ten purses of gold: da┼Ыa ko┼Ыaiс╕е suvarс╣Зa p┼лrс╣Зam da┼Ыako┼Ы─Бn, the ten bags or chests full of gold;

Atithigva: prastoka, divod─Бsa and atithigva, are different names of the same person n, a r─Бj─Б, the son of Sс╣Ы├▒jaya

Jamison Brereton

Prastoka from your bounty, Indra, has just now given ten casks, ten prizewinners.
From Divod─Бsa, (son?) of Atithigva, we have accepted as bounty the goods belonging to ┼Ъambara.

Jamison Brereton Notes

k├│┼Ыay─л- is a hapax; its difference, if any, from well-attested k├│┼Ыa-, which also appears in the following vs., in the same number of тАШtenтАЩ, canтАЩt be determined.

Griffith

Out of thy bounty, Indra, hath Prastoka bestowed ten coffers and ten mettled horses.
We have received in turn from Divodasa Sambara’s wealth, the gift of Atithigva.

Geldner

Prastoka hat von deiner Ehrengabe, Indra, zehn Truhen, zehn Preisrenner geschenkt. Von Divodasa als Lohn bekommen.

Grassmann

Prastoka gab nun von deinem Schatz, o Indra, zehn Truhen voll und zehn schnelle Rosse; von Divodasa empfingen wir des Atithigva Geschenk und das dem ├Зambara genommene Gut.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ ! рдпрд╕реНрддреЗ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдиреЛ рд░рд╛рдзрд╕реЛ рджрд╢ рдХреЛрд╢рдпреАрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреЛрдХреЛрд╜рджрд╛рддреНред рджрд╢рдЧреБрдгрдВ рд╕рдореНрдкрд╛рджрдпрддрд┐ рдпрджрддрд┐рдерд┐рдЧреНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рджрд┐рд╡реЛрджрд╛рд╕рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рд░рд╛рдзрдГ рд╢рд╛рдореНрдмрд░рдВ рд╡рд╕реБ рдЪ рд╡рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧреНрд░рднреАрд╖реНрдо рддрджрд┐рдиреНрдиреБ рднрд╡рд╛рдирд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рддрджрд┐рдиреНрдиреБ рд╡рдпрдВ рддреБрднреНрдпрдВ рджрджреНрдпрд╛рдо реереиреирее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрддреМ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреМ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреЗрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Griffith

Ten horses and ten treasure-chests, ten garments as an added gift,
These and ten lumps of gold have I received from Divodasa’s hand.

Zehn Pferde, zehn Kasten, zehn Kleider als Zugabe, zehn Goldklumpen erhielt ich von Divodasa.

English translation:

тАЬThe son of Sс╣Ы├▒jaya has reverenced the Bharadv─Бjas who have accepted such great wealth for the good of all men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The descendant of Sr╠е├▒jaya has reached toward the Bharadv─Бjas, who have acquired great bounty belonging to all people.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb abhy ├аyaс╣гс╣нa is problematic, at least in my view. It is supposed to be the 3rd sg. mid. root aor. to тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ. The form is morphologically impeccable, but 1) abh├н is not found with тИЪyaj anywhere else in the RV, or indeed in Vedic; 2) for тИЪyaj тАШsacrifice toтАЩ to take an acc. of humans, rather than the standard gods, is skirting blasphemy. In this passage it is said to mean тАШhonorтАЩ, but it is hard to see how the ubiquitous root тИЪyaj could be so bleached, nor why the addition of the preverb abh├н would effect this change. The published translation тАЬhas reached towardsтАЭ reflects a different analysis. I suggest that it actually belongs to the root aor. of тИЪ(n)a┼Ы тАШreach, attainтАЩ, which does appear fairly regularly with abh├н. A putative injunc. in this lexeme, *abh(├н)y aс╣гс╣нa, could have produced a segmentation *abh├н-yaс╣гс╣нa, and in turn an augmented form abh├н ayaс╣гс╣нa could have been generated to it. The sense of the passage might be similar to the current (annoying) English idiom тАЬreach out to,тАЭ meaning тАЬproactively contact in a positive way,тАЭ and refer to the S─Бr├▒jayaтАЩs transfer of goods to the Bharadv─Бja poets. However, I recognize that it is generally preferable not to posit such a morphological misunderstanding and reformation, and also that my semantic substitution isnтАЩt altogether compelling. Michael Weiss suggests an alternative etymology, connecting it to y├б┼Ыas- тАШgloryтАЩ, etc. and taking it as a med. root formation meaning тАШmade famous, ennobled, glorifiedтАЩ. Both the morphology and the root semantics would work, though I am somewhat skeptical that a middle formation of that sort would have transitive-factitive sense.

Thus Srnjaya’s son honoured the Bharadvajas, recipients of all noble gifts and bounty.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Chariot made of the) forest lord, be strong of fabric; be our friend; be our protector, and be manned by warriors; you are wrapped with cow-hides; keep us steady; and may he who rides in you be victorious over conquered (foes).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Be manned by warriors: suv─лro bhava = ┼Ы┼лrabhaс╣нt.aiс╕е putr─Бdibhir v─Б yuktaс╕е, joined with warriors, or with sons and the rest; you are wrapped with cow-hides: gobhiс╕е sannaddhosi = you are bound together by cow; govik─Бraiс╕е, by what are formed from cattle; in the next с╣Ыca, gobhir─Бvс╣Ыtam = carmabhiс╕е parita aveс╣гс╣нitam, encompassed round with hides, as if the exterior of the war-chariot especially were so strengthened; or, encompassed with rays of light, or with splendours, gobhiс╕е, tejobhiс╕е

Jamison Brereton

O tree, because you should become firm-limbed, a comrade to us, furthering (us), affording good heroes,
you are knotted together with cows [=leather (straps)]. Be firm! Let the one who mounts you win what is to be won.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWorship with oblations the chariot constructed of the substance of heaven and earth, the extracted essence of the forest lords; the velocity of the waters; the encompassed with the cow-hide; the thunderbolt (of Indra).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Strength has been brought up from heaven, from earth; might has been brought here from the trees.
To the strongness of the waters enclosed by cows, to the mace of
IndraтАФto the ChariotтАФsacrifice with an oblation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The awkward тАШstrongnessтАЩ in English tr. is meant to represent the difference between ├│jas- тАШstrengthтАЩ in p─Бda a, the standard nominal abstract to this root, and ojm├бn-, found only here in the RV, though attested in subsequent Vedic texts. Although the ref. to the chariot in vs. 26 is hardly transparent, in this vs. it has become a barely solvable riddle. In particular, тАЬthe strongness of the waters enclosed by cowsтАЭ (ap─Б╠Бm ojm─Б╠Бnam p├бri g├│bhir ─Б╠Бvс╣Ыtam) could not be interpr. without 26a, c: the тАЬstrongness of the watersтАЭ is presumably the tree (v├бnas-p├бti- in 26a, 27b), or rather the wood of the tree – so called because plants grow only when watered.

тАЬEnclosed by cowsтАЭ recalls 26c тАЬknotted together with cowsтАЩ (hide)тАЭ (g├│bhiс╕е s├бс╣Гnaddhaс╕е), referring to the leather that binds the wooden parts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. are repeated in the A┼Ыvamedha section of several early Vedic ritual texts, directly after the 1st 14 vss. of the weapon hymn VI.75 (e.g., VS XXIX.52-57, TS IV.6.6.

Griffith

Its mighty strength was borrowed from the heaven and earth: its conquering force was brought from sovrans of the wood.
Honour with holy gifts the Car like Indra’s bolt, the Car bound round with straps, the vigour of the floods.

Geldner

Von Himmel und Erde ward die Kraft entnommen, von den B├дumen ist seine St├дrke genommen. Die Wucht der Gew├дsser, die mit Rindsleder bezogen ist, des Indra Donnerkeil, den Wagen verehre mit Opfergabe!

Grassmann

Die von der Erde und dem Himmel entnommene Kraft, die von den B├дumen hergenommene St├дrke, die Macht der Gew├дsser, den mit Riemen umgebenen Wagen, der schnell ist wie Indra’s Blitz, den verehre mit Opferguss.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDo you, divine chariot, who are the thunderbolt of Indra, the precursor of the Maruts, the embryo of Mitra, the navel of Varuс╣Зa, propitiated by this our sacrifice, accept the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The precursor of Maruts: marut─Бm an─лkam mitrasya garbho varuс╣Зasya n─Бbhiс╕е: an─лkam = agrabh┼лtam, being before, out-stripping in speed; or, mukhyam, principal or leader; garbha of Mitra: the car is said to be contained by Mitra, the ruler of the day, as moving by day; n─Бbhi of Varuс╣Зa: it is a fixed point or centre for the deity ruling over the night, when the car of Indra or S┼лrya stands still; another interpretation: garbha is from gс╣Ы, to praise; mitrasya garbha = s┼лryeс╣Зa st┼лyam─Бna, to be praised by the sun; n─Бbhi is from n─Бbh, to injure; hence, the weapon of Varuс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

The mace of Indra, the face of the Maruts, the embryo of Mitra, the navel of Varuс╣ЗaтАФ
taking pleasure in this oblation-giving of ours, god Chariot, accept our oblations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Why the chariot is all the things itтАЩs implicitly identified with in ab is not entirely clear: it is the mace of Indra presumably because it performs similar assaults, and the face of the Maruts presumably because its front is as glittery and fast-moving as they are. But the Mitra and Varuс╣Зa identifications elude me.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. are repeated in the A┼Ыvamedha section of several early Vedic ritual texts, directly after the 1st 14 vss. of the weapon hymn VI.75 (e.g., VS XXIX.52-57, TS IV.6.6.

Griffith

Thou Bolt of Indra, Vanguard of the Maruts, close knit to Varuna and Child of Mitra,-
As such, accepting gifts which here we offer, receive, O Godlike Chariot, these oblations.

Geldner

Des Indra Donnerkeil, die Heeresspitze der Marut, das Kind des Mitra, des Varuna Nabel bist du. La├Я dir diesen Opferanteil von uns gefallen; nimm, du g├╢ttlicher Wagen, die Opfergaben an!

Grassmann

Des Indra Blitz du, der Maruts Glanzerscheinung, des Mitra Spross, des Varuna Verwandter, o Wagen, diese unsre Opfergabe annehmend, ergreife, o Gott, diese Opfer.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWar-drum, fill with your sound both heaven and earth; and let all things, fixed or moveable, be aware of it; do you, who are associated with Indra and the gods, drive away our foes to the remotest distance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Make Heaven and Earth gasp. Let the moving (world [=living
creatures]) dispersed in many places pay attention to you.
O Drum, along with Indra, with the gods, drive away the rivals farther than far. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

These vss. are repeated in the A┼Ыvamedha section of several early Vedic ritual texts, directly after the 1st 14 vss. of the weapon hymn VI.75 (e.g., VS XXIX.52-57, TS IV.6.6.

Griffith

Send forth thy voice aloud through earth and heaven, and let the world in all its breadth regard thee;
O Drum, accordant with the Gods and Indra, drive thou afar, yea, very far, our foemen.

Geldner

Mach die Erde und den Himmel erdr├╢hnen! Die vielerorts verbreitete Kreatur soll deiner gedenken. Im Verein mit Indra und den G├╢ttern vertreibe du Pauke die Feinde in fernste Ferne!

Grassmann

Auf, schnaube an die Erde und den Himmel, dein nehme wahr ringsum die ausgedehnte Welt; o Pauke, du mit Indra und den G├╢ttern vereint verjage weit hinweg die Feinde.

English translation:

тАЬSound loud against the (hostile) host; animate our prowess; thunder aloud, terrifying the evil-minded; rapid, drum, those whose delight is to harm us; you are the fist of Indra; inspire us with fierceness.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRecover these our cattle, Indra; bring them back; the drum sounds repeatedly as a signal; our leaders, mounted on their steeds, assemble; may our warriors, riding in their cars, Indra, be victorious.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 29, 55-57 has this and thr preceding two с╣Ыcas

Jamison Brereton

Drive those yonder [=cows] hither and make the ones here turn back. The Drum keeps speaking, giving the signal.
Our men, with horses as their wings, are converging: (so) let our
charioteers win, o Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner explains p─Бda a persuasively as тАЬRaub und Wiederraub der K├╝he,тАЭ with the тАШyonder onesтАЩ (am┼л╠Бс╕е) those belonging to the enemy and the ones here (im─Б╠Бс╕е) our own.

I do not understand why c├бranti is accented. Geldner takes it as implicitly subordinated (тАЬWenn тАж sich sammelnтАЭ), which would account for the accent, but thereтАЩs no other evidence for subordination. It could be ascribed to the vague principle that the verb is accented in a clause that provides the basis for the next clause, as Oldenberg suggests only to question (ZDMG 60: 725 n. 1 = KlSch. p. 200).

Our heroes, winged with horses, come together. Let our car-warriors, Indra, be triumphant.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдЬрди рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдХрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ рее

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреАрд░реНрдг рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреН ! рдЖрдк рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рджреБрдиреНрджреБрднрд┐рдГ) рдирдЧрд╛реЬрд╛ (рдХреЗрддреБрдорддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╡рд╛рд╡рджреАрддрд┐) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдмрдЬрд╛рддрд╛, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рдЗрдорд╛рдГ) рдпрд╣ (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рдиреН рдкрдХреНрд╖реЛрдВрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдЕрдкрдиреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдПрдБ (рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдп) рд▓реМрдЯрд╛рдЗрдпреЗ рдФрд░ рдЙрдирд╕реЗ (рдЕрдореВрдГ) рдпрд╣ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдПрдБ рджреВрд░ (рдЖ, рдЕрдЬ) рдлреЗрдВрдХрд┐рдпреЗ рдЬреЛ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ (рд░рдерд┐рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рд░рдерд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рдирд░рдГ) рдирд╛рдпрдХ рд╡реАрд░ рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЬрдпрдиреНрддреБ) рдЬреАрддреЗрдВ рдФрд░ рдЬреЛ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдп рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕рдореН, рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐) рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рд╡рд┐рдЪрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕реБрд╢реЛрднрд┐рдд рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерейрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдорд┐рддреНрд░, рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдп, рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛, рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА, рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдорд╛рдиреН, рд╡рд╛рдгреА, рд╕рддреНрдп, рдмрд▓, рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо, рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдБрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рджреБрдиреНрджреБрднрд┐рдГ рдХреЗрддреБрдорджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рджреАрддрд┐ рддрдереЗрдорд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдп рддрд╛рднрд┐рд░рдореВрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛ рджреВрд░ рдЖрдЬред рдпреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд░рдерд┐рдиреЛ рдирд░реЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдЮреНрдЬрдпрдиреНрддреБред рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрд╛рдп рд╕рдВрдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдирд▓рдВрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ реерейрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рджрдпреЛ рдЬрдирд╛рдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреНрдпреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЖ) (рдЕрдореВрдГ) рдЗрдорд╛рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдГ (рдЕрдЬ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреНрджреВрд░реЗ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдк (рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдп) (рдЗрдорд╛рдГ) рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрд╛рдГ (рдХреЗрддреБрдорддреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН (рджреБрдиреНрджреБрднрд┐рдГ) (рд╡рд╛рд╡рджреАрддрд┐) рднреГрд╢рдВ рд╡рджрддрд┐ (рд╕рдореН) (рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ) рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдкрд░реНрдгрд╛рдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ (рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдирд░рдГ) рдирд╛рдпрдХрд╛рдГ (рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН) (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░рдХ (рд░рдерд┐рдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рд╕реНрддрд╛ рд░рдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рддреЗ (рдЬрдпрдиреНрддреБ) реерейрезрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рджрдпреЛ рдЬрдирд╛ рдпреВрдпрдВ рджреБрдиреНрджреБрднреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд░рднреВрд╖рд┐рддрд╛ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрджреВрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдкрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рддреНрдп рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпреЗрдг рдкрд╛рд▓рдпрддреЗрддрд┐ реерейрезрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╕реЛрдордкреНрд░рд╢реНрдиреЛрддреНрддрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реЗрдирд╛рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд░рдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдзреНрдпрд╛рдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реЛрдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдореЗрдШрд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╡реАрд░рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдпрд╛рдирдпрдЬреНрдЮрдорд┐рддреНрд░реИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреНрдпрдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрдиреНрдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реАрд╡рд╛рдХреНрд╕рддреНрдпрдмрд▓рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдорд░рд╛рдЬрдиреАрддрд┐-рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд╢рддреНрд░реБрдЬрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорддреНрдкрд░рдорд╣рдВрд╕рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬрдХрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд░рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЖрд░реНрдпреНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рднреВрд╖рд┐рдд рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдерд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдХреЗ рд╕рдкреНрддрдореЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрдГ, рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГ, рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рд╕рдкреНрддрдЪрддреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдВрдиреЛ ! рддреБрдореНрд╣реА рджреБрдиреНрджреБрднрд┐ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рднреВрд╖рд┐рдд рдЕрд╕рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд╡ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рд┐рдд рдЕрд╕рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рд╕реЗрдиреЗрджреНрд╡рд╛рд░реЗ рджреВрд░ рдЕрд╕рд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдВрдирд╛рд╣реА рдЬрд┐рдВрдХреВрди рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрдЪреЗ рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рдиреЗ рдкрд╛рд▓рди рдХрд░рд╛. рее рейрез рее
